<p><b>Shenzhen</b> (<span class="IPA" style="white-space:nowrap"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA_for_Mandarin" title="Help:IPA for Mandarin">[ʂə́nʈʂə̂n]</a></span><small class="nowrap metadata"> (<a href="/wiki/File:Shenzhen_pronunciation.ogg" title="File:Shenzhen pronunciation.ogg"><img alt="" data-file-height="500" data-file-width="500" height="13" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/21/Speaker_Icon.svg/13px-Speaker_Icon.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/21/Speaker_Icon.svg/20px-Speaker_Icon.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/21/Speaker_Icon.svg/26px-Speaker_Icon.svg.png 2x" width="13"/></a> <a class="internal" href="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/4/47/Shenzhen_pronunciation.ogg" title="Shenzhen pronunciation.ogg">listen</a>)</small>; <a href="/wiki/Chinese_language" title="Chinese language">Chinese</a>: <span lang="zh">深圳</span><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-3"><a href="#cite_note-3">[3]</a></sup>) is a major city in <a href="/wiki/Guangdong" title="Guangdong">Guangdong</a> Province, <a href="/wiki/China" title="China">China</a>. The city is located immediately north of <a href="/wiki/Hong_Kong" title="Hong Kong">Hong Kong</a> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Special_Administrative_Region_(China)" title="Special Administrative Region (China)">Special Administrative Region</a> and holds <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sub-provincial" title="Sub-provincial">sub-provincial</a> administrative status, with powers slightly less than a province.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-4"><a href="#cite_note-4">[4]</a></sup></p>
<p>Shenzhen was a market town of 30,000 people on the route of the <a href="/wiki/Kowloon%E2%80%93Canton_Railway" title="Kowloon–Canton Railway">Kowloon–Canton Railway</a>. That changed in 1979 when Shenzhen was promoted to city-status and in 1980 designated China’s first <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Special_Economic_Zones_of_the_People%27s_Republic_of_China" title="Special Economic Zones of the People's Republic of China">Special Economic Zone</a> (SEZ).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-5"><a href="#cite_note-5">[5]</a></sup> According to the Government report for 2015, Shenzhen had transformed into a city with a population of 10,778,900<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-6"><a href="#cite_note-6">[6]</a></sup> and a metropolitan area population of over 18 million. Shenzhen was one of the fastest-growing cities in the world during the 1990s and the 2000s.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-7"><a href="#cite_note-7">[7]</a></sup> Shenzhen's population boom slowed down to less than one percent per year by 2013 as the manufacturing boom ebbed in favor of other industries.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-8"><a href="#cite_note-8">[8]</a></sup></p>
<p>Shenzhen's modern cityscape is the result of its vibrant economy made possible by rapid <a href="/wiki/Foreign_direct_investment" title="Foreign direct investment">foreign investment</a> since the institution of the policy of "<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Reform_and_opening" title="Reform and opening">reform and opening</a>" establishment of the SEZ in late 1979.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-9"><a href="#cite_note-9">[9]</a></sup></p>
<p>Shenzhen is a major financial center in southern China. The city is home to the <a href="/wiki/Shenzhen_Stock_Exchange" title="Shenzhen Stock Exchange">Shenzhen Stock Exchange</a> as well as the headquarters of numerous high-tech companies.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-10"><a href="#cite_note-10">[10]</a></sup> Shenzhen ranks 19th in the 2016 edition of the <a href="/wiki/Global_Financial_Centres_Index" title="Global Financial Centres Index">Global Financial Centres Index</a> published by the <a href="/wiki/Z/Yen" title="Z/Yen">Z/Yen Group</a> and <a href="/wiki/Qatar_Financial_Centre" title="Qatar Financial Centre">Qatar Financial Centre Authority</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-GFCI_11-0"><a href="#cite_note-GFCI-11">[11]</a></sup> It also has one of the <a href="/wiki/List_of_busiest_container_ports" title="List of busiest container ports">busiest container ports</a> in the world.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-12"><a href="#cite_note-12">[12]</a></sup></p>
<p></p>

<p></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Shenzhen&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Human habitation in Shenzhen dates back to ancient times. The earliest archaeological remains so far unearthed are shards from a site at Xiantouling on <a href="/wiki/Mirs_Bay" title="Mirs Bay">Dapeng Bay</a>, dating back to 5000 BC. From the <a href="/wiki/Han_dynasty" title="Han dynasty">Han dynasty</a> (third century BC) onwards, the area around Shenzhen was a center of the salt monopoly, thus meriting special Imperial protection. Salt pans are still visible around the Pearl River area to the west of the city and are commemorated in the name of <a href="/wiki/Yantian_District" title="Yantian District">Yantian District</a> (<span lang="zh-hans">盐田</span>, meaning "salt fields").<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-szmc_13-0"><a href="#cite_note-szmc-13">[13]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-szmc2_14-0"><a href="#cite_note-szmc2-14">[14]</a></sup></p>
<p>The settlement at <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Nantou_(historical_town)" title="Nantou (historical town)">Nantou</a> was the political center of the area from early antiquity. In the year 331 AD, six counties covering most of modern southeastern Guangdong were merged into one province or “jun” (郡) named Dongguan with its administrative center at Nantou.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-szmc_13-1"><a href="#cite_note-szmc-13">[13]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-szmc2_14-1"><a href="#cite_note-szmc2-14">[14]</a></sup> As well as being a center of the politically and fiscally critical salt trade, the area had strategic importance as a stopping off point for international trade. The main shipping route to <a href="/wiki/India" title="India">India</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Arabia" title="Arabia">Arabia</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Byzantine_Empire" title="Byzantine Empire">Byzantine Empire</a> started at <a href="/wiki/Guangzhou" title="Guangzhou">Guangzhou</a>. As early as the eighth century, chronicles record the Nantou area as being a major commercial center, and reported that all foreign ships in the Guangzhou trade would stop there. It was also as a naval defense center guarding the southern approaches to the Pearl River.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-autogenerated1_15-0"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated1-15">[15]</a></sup></p>
<p>Shenzhen was also involved in the events surrounding the end of the <a href="/wiki/Song_dynasty" title="Song dynasty">Southern Song dynasty</a> (1276–79). The Imperial court, fleeing <a href="/wiki/Kublai_Khan" title="Kublai Khan">Kublai Khan</a>’s forces, established itself in the Shenzhen area. <a href="/wiki/Lu_Xiufu" title="Lu Xiufu">Lu Xiufu</a>, the then-chief minister, realized all was lost and knowing the Mongolian forces would soon take over the area, he preferred suicide instead of the emperor being captured which might have brought shame to the dynasty.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-szmc_13-2"><a href="#cite_note-szmc-13">[13]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-szmc2_14-2"><a href="#cite_note-szmc2-14">[14]</a></sup> He jumped off a cliff with <a href="/wiki/Emperor_Bing_of_Song" title="Emperor Bing of Song">Emperor Bing</a>, aged 7, the last emperor of the Southern Song Dynasty strapped to his back, killing both. In the late 19th century the Chiu or Zhao (Zhao was also the Song Imperial surname) clan in Hong Kong identified that <a href="/wiki/Chiwan" title="Chiwan">Chiwan</a> (Chinese:赤湾), an area near <a href="/wiki/Shekou" title="Shekou">Shekou</a> as the final resting place of the Emperor and built a tomb for him. The tomb, since restored, is still at the same location.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-16"><a href="#cite_note-16">[16]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:%E5%BE%80%E6%B7%B1%E5%9C%B3.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1920" data-file-width="2560" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b7/%E5%BE%80%E6%B7%B1%E5%9C%B3.JPG/220px-%E5%BE%80%E6%B7%B1%E5%9C%B3.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b7/%E5%BE%80%E6%B7%B1%E5%9C%B3.JPG/330px-%E5%BE%80%E6%B7%B1%E5%9C%B3.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b7/%E5%BE%80%E6%B7%B1%E5%9C%B3.JPG/440px-%E5%BE%80%E6%B7%B1%E5%9C%B3.JPG 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:%E5%BE%80%E6%B7%B1%E5%9C%B3.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
An old Hong Kong railway sign rendering the city's name as "Shum Chun"</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Earliest known records that carried the name <i>Shenzhen</i> dates from 1410, during the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ming_Dynasty" title="Ming Dynasty">Ming Dynasty</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-17"><a href="#cite_note-17">[17]</a></sup> Local people called the drains in paddy fields “zhen” (<span lang="zh"><a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/%E5%9C%B3" title="wikt:圳">圳</a></span>). Shenzhen (<span lang="zh">深圳</span>) literally means “deep drains” as the area was once crisscrossed with rivers and streams, with deep drains within the paddy fields. The character <span lang="zh">圳</span> is limited in distribution to an area of South China with its most northerly examples in Zhejiang Province which suggests an association with southwards migration during the Southern Song Dynasty (12th and 13th centuries).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-18"><a href="#cite_note-18">[18]</a></sup> The County town at Xin'an in modern Nanshan dates from the Ming Dynasty where it was a major naval center at the mouth of the Pearl River. In this capacity it was heavily involved in 1521 in the successful Chinese action against the Portuguese Fleet under <a href="/wiki/Fern%C3%A3o_Pires_de_Andrade" title="Fernão Pires de Andrade">Fernão Pires de Andrade</a>. This battle, called the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/First_Battle_of_Tamao_(1521)" title="First Battle of Tamao (1521)">Battle of Tunmen</a>, was fought in the straits between <a href="/wiki/Shekou" title="Shekou">Shekou</a> and <a href="/wiki/Nei_Lingding_Island" title="Nei Lingding Island">Nei Lingding Island</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-autogenerated1_15-1"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated1-15">[15]</a></sup></p>
<p>In November 1979, <a href="/wiki/Bao%27an_County" title="Bao'an County">Bao'an County</a> (<span lang="zh-hans">宝安县</span>) was promoted to <a href="/wiki/Prefecture" title="Prefecture">prefecture</a> level, directly governed by <a href="/wiki/Guangdong" title="Guangdong">Guangdong</a> province. It was renamed Shenzhen, after Shenzhen town, the then administrative centre of the county which stood approximately around present location of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Dongmen_Subdistrict,_Shenzhen" title="Dongmen Subdistrict, Shenzhen">Dongmen</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-szmc_13-3"><a href="#cite_note-szmc-13">[13]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-szmc2_14-3"><a href="#cite_note-szmc2-14">[14]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="1980_onwards_as_a_Special_Economic_Zone">1980 onwards as a Special Economic Zone</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Shenzhen&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: 1980 onwards as a Special Economic Zone">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Shenzhen was singled out to be the first of the five <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Special_Economic_Zones_of_the_People%27s_Republic_of_China" title="Special Economic Zones of the People's Republic of China">Special Economic Zones</a> (SEZ) in May 1980. Initially, the SEZ comprises an area of only 327.5 km<sup>2</sup> of southern Shenzhen, covering the current <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Luohu" title="Luohu">Luohu</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Futian" title="Futian">Futian</a>, <a href="/wiki/Nanshan_District,_Shenzhen" title="Nanshan District, Shenzhen">Nanshan</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Yantian" title="Yantian">Yantian</a> districts. The SEZ was created to be an experimental ground for the practice of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Market_capitalism" title="Market capitalism">market capitalism</a> within a community guided by the ideals of "<a href="/wiki/Socialist_market_economy" title="Socialist market economy">socialism with Chinese characteristics</a>".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Economist_19-0"><a href="#cite_note-Economist-19">[19]</a></sup></p>
<p>In 1982 <a href="/wiki/Bao%27an_County" title="Bao'an County">Bao'an County</a> was re-established, though this time as a part of Shenzhen. The county was converted to become <a href="/wiki/Bao%27an_District" title="Bao'an District">Bao'an District</a>, which was out of the Special Economic Zone. Shenzhen was promoted to a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sub-provincial_City" title="Sub-provincial City">Sub-provincial City</a> in March 1983 and was given the right of provincial-level economic administration in November 1988.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-szmc_13-4"><a href="#cite_note-szmc-13">[13]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-szmc2_14-4"><a href="#cite_note-szmc2-14">[14]</a></sup> With a population of 30,000 in 1980, economic development has meant that by 2008 the city has had 12 million inhabitants.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-20"><a href="#cite_note-20">[20]</a></sup></p>
<p>Shenzhen became one of the largest cities in the <a href="/wiki/Pearl_River_Delta" title="Pearl River Delta">Pearl River Delta</a> region, which itself is an economic hub of China, as well as the largest manufacturing base in the world.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-21"><a href="#cite_note-21">[21]</a></sup></p>
<p>For five months in 1996, Shenzhen was home to the <a href="/wiki/Provisional_Legislative_Council" title="Provisional Legislative Council">Provisional Legislative Council</a> and <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Provisional_Executive_Council_of_Hong_Kong&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Provisional Executive Council of Hong Kong (page does not exist)">Provisional Executive Council</a> of Hong Kong.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-22"><a href="#cite_note-22">[22]</a></sup></p>
<p>On 1 July 2010, the Shenzhen Special Economic Zone was expanded to include all districts, a five-fold increase over its pre-expansion size. In August 2011, the city hosted the <a href="/wiki/2011_Summer_Universiade" title="2011 Summer Universiade">26th Universiade</a>, an international multi-sport event organized for university athletes.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-23"><a href="#cite_note-23">[23]</a></sup></p>

<p>Shenzhen is located within the <a href="/wiki/Pearl_River_Delta" title="Pearl River Delta">Pearl River Delta</a>, bordering Hong Kong to the south, Huizhou to the north and northeast, <a href="/wiki/Dongguan" title="Dongguan">Dongguan</a> to the north and northwest. <a href="/wiki/Lingdingyang" title="Lingdingyang">Lingdingyang</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Pearl_River,_China" title="Pearl River, China">Pearl River</a> to the west and <a href="/wiki/Mirs_Bay" title="Mirs Bay">Mirs Bay</a> to the east and roughly 100 kilometres (62 mi) southeast of the provincial capital of <a href="/wiki/Guangzhou" title="Guangzhou">Guangzhou</a>. The municipality covers an area of 1,991.64 square kilometres (769 sq mi) including urban and rural areas, with a total population of 10,358,381 at the 2010 census.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-citypopulation.de_24-0"><a href="#cite_note-citypopulation.de-24">[24]</a></sup> It makes up part of Pearl Delta River built-up area with 44,738,513 inhabitants, spread over 9 municipalities (including <a href="/wiki/Macau" title="Macau">Macau</a>). The city is elongated measuring 81.4 kilometers from east to west while the shortest section from north to south is 10.8 kilometers.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-25"><a href="#cite_note-25">[25]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Rivers_and_Reservoirs">Rivers and Reservoirs</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Shenzhen&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Rivers and Reservoirs">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Over 160 rivers or channels flow through Shenzhen. There are currently 24 reservoirs within the city limits with a total capacity of 525 million tonnes.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-26"><a href="#cite_note-26">[26]</a></sup></p>
<p>Notable rivers in Shenzhen include the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Shenzhen_River" title="Shenzhen River">Shenzhen River</a>, Maozhou River and Longgang River.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-27"><a href="#cite_note-27">[27]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Islands">Islands</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Shenzhen&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Islands">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">See also: <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/List_of_Islands_in_Shenzhen" title="List of Islands in Shenzhen">List of Islands in Shenzhen</a></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Climate">Climate</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Shenzhen&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Climate">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Although Shenzhen is situated about a degree south of the <a href="/wiki/Tropic_of_Cancer" title="Tropic of Cancer">Tropic of Cancer</a>, due to the Siberian anticyclone, it has a warm, <a href="/wiki/Monsoon" title="Monsoon">monsoon</a>-influenced, <a href="/wiki/Humid_subtropical_climate" title="Humid subtropical climate">humid subtropical climate</a> (<a href="/wiki/K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification" title="Köppen climate classification">Köppen</a> <i>Cwa</i>). Winters are mild and relatively dry, due in part to the influence of the <a href="/wiki/South_China_Sea" title="South China Sea">South China Sea</a>, and frost is very rare; it begins dry but becomes progressively more humid and overcast. However, fog is most frequent in winter and spring, with 106 days per year reporting some fog. Early spring is the cloudiest time of year, and rainfall begins to dramatically increase in April; the rainy season lasts until late September to early October. The monsoon reaches its peak intensity in the summer months, when the city also experiences very humid, and hot, but moderated, conditions; there are only 2.4 days of 35 °C (95 °F)+ temperatures.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-SZMB_via_21CMA_28-0"><a href="#cite_note-SZMB_via_21CMA-28">[28]</a></sup> The region is prone to torrential rain as well, with 9.7 days that have 50 mm (1.97 in) or more of rain, and 2.2 days of at least 100 mm (3.94 in).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-SZMB_via_21CMA_28-1"><a href="#cite_note-SZMB_via_21CMA-28">[28]</a></sup> The latter portion of autumn is dry. The annual precipitation averages at around 1,970 mm (78 in), some of which is delivered in <a href="/wiki/Typhoon" title="Typhoon">typhoons</a> that strike from the east during summer and early autumn. Extreme temperatures have ranged from 0.2 °C (32 °F) on 11 February 1957 to 38.7 °C (102 °F) on 10 July 1980.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Mherrera_29-0"><a href="#cite_note-Mherrera-29">[29]</a></sup></p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Administrative_divisions">Administrative divisions</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Shenzhen&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Administrative divisions">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/List_of_administrative_divisions_of_Shenzhen" title="List of administrative divisions of Shenzhen">List of administrative divisions of Shenzhen</a></div>

<td>qin4 hoi2</td>

<p>The Special Economic Zone (SEZ) comprised only <a href="/wiki/Luohu_District" title="Luohu District">Luohu</a>, <a href="/wiki/Futian_District" title="Futian District">Futian</a>, <a href="/wiki/Nanshan_District,_Shenzhen" title="Nanshan District, Shenzhen">Nanshan</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Yantian_District" title="Yantian District">Yantian</a> districts until 1 July 2010, when the SEZ was expanded to include all the other districts, a five-fold increase over its pre-expansion size.</p>
<p>Adjacent to Hong Kong in southern China, Luohu is the financial and trading center of Shenzhen. Futian, at the heart of the SEZ, is the seat of the Municipal Government. West of Futian, Nanshan is the center for high-tech industries. Formerly outside the SEZ, Bao'an and Longgang are located to the north-west and north-east, respectively, of central Shenzhen. Yantian is the location of Yantian Port, the second busiest <a href="/wiki/Container_terminal" title="Container terminal">container terminal</a> in mainland China and the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/List_of_world%27s_busiest_container_ports" title="List of world's busiest container ports">third busiest</a> in the world.</p>
<div style="clear:both;"></div>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Demographics">Demographics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Shenzhen&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Demographics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tmulti tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:608px;max-width:608px">
<div style="clear:both;font-weight:bold;text-align:center;background-color:transparent">Graphics</div>
<div class="tsingle" style="float:left;margin:1px;width:302px;max-width:302px">
<div class="thumbimage"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Shenzhen,_China,_city_population_dynamics.png"><img alt="" data-file-height="916" data-file-width="959" height="287" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6c/Shenzhen%2C_China%2C_city_population_dynamics.png/300px-Shenzhen%2C_China%2C_city_population_dynamics.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6c/Shenzhen%2C_China%2C_city_population_dynamics.png/450px-Shenzhen%2C_China%2C_city_population_dynamics.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6c/Shenzhen%2C_China%2C_city_population_dynamics.png/600px-Shenzhen%2C_China%2C_city_population_dynamics.png 2x" width="300"/></a></div>

<p>Shenzhen has seen its population and activity develop rapidly since the establishment of the SEZ. Shenzhen has a population of over ten million. About six million of these people are non-local migrant workers who may return to their home town/city on the weekends and live in factory dormitories during the week. Shenzhen is the largest migrant city in China.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-36"><a href="#cite_note-36">[36]</a></sup></p>
<p>There had been migration into southern Guangdong province and what is now Shenzhen since the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Southern_Song_dynasty" title="Southern Song dynasty">Southern Song dynasty</a> (1127–1279) but the numbers increased dramatically since Shenzhen was established in the 1980s. In Guangdong province, it is the only city where the local language, Cantonese, Hakka, or Teochew, is not the main language; it is <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Standard_Mandarin" title="Standard Mandarin">Mandarin</a> that is mostly spoken, with migrants from all over China. At present, the average age in Shenzhen is less than 30. The age range is as follows: 8.49% between the age of 0 and 14, 88.41% between the age of 15 and 59, and 3.1% aged 65 or above.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-37"><a href="#cite_note-37">[37]</a></sup></p>
<p>The population structure polarizes into two opposing extremes: intellectuals with a high level of education, and migrant workers with poor education.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-SZGov_38-0"><a href="#cite_note-SZGov-38">[38]</a></sup> It was reported in June 2007 that over 20 percent of P.R.C's PhD's worked in Shenzhen.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-39"><a href="#cite_note-39">[39]</a></sup></p>
<p>According to the <a href="/wiki/Hong_Kong_General_Chamber_of_Commerce" title="Hong Kong General Chamber of Commerce">Hong Kong General Chamber of Commerce</a>, in 2002, 7,200 Hong Kong residents commuted daily to Shenzhen for work, and 2,200 students from Shenzhen commuted to school in Hong Kong.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (December 2016)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> Though neighboring each other, daily commuters still need to pass through customs and immigration checkpoints, as travel between the SEZ and the Hong Kong <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Special_Administrative_Region_of_the_People%27s_Republic_of_China" title="Special Administrative Region of the People's Republic of China">Special Administrative Region</a> (SAR) is restricted.</p>
<p>In late July 2003, <a href="/wiki/China" title="China">China</a> relaxed travel restrictions to allow individuals from the southern cities of <a href="/wiki/Guangzhou" title="Guangzhou">Guangzhou</a> and Shenzhen, as well as Beijing and Shanghai, to visit Hong Kong. Previously, <a href="/wiki/Mainland_China" title="Mainland China">mainland</a> travelers could only visit the city as part of tour groups. (See <a href="/wiki/Individual_Visit_Scheme" title="Individual Visit Scheme">Individual Visit Scheme</a>.)</p>
<p>Immigration into Shenzhen from China's interior was previously restricted by the <i><a href="/wiki/Hukou_system" title="Hukou system">hukou</a></i> system. One consequence is that just outside Shenzhen, there exist large towns consisting of now settled migrants who had previously attempted to enter the city.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Religion">Religion</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Shenzhen&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Religion">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>According to 2010 data collected by a <a href="/wiki/University_of_Southern_California" title="University of Southern California">University of Southern California</a> research project, approximately 37% of Shenzhen residents were practitioners of <a href="/wiki/Chinese_folk_religion" title="Chinese folk religion">Chinese folk religions</a>, 26% are <a href="/wiki/Buddhism" title="Buddhism">Buddhists</a>, 18% <a href="/wiki/Taoism" title="Taoism">Taoists</a>, 2% <a href="/wiki/Christian" title="Christian">Christians</a> and 2% <a href="/wiki/Muslim" title="Muslim">Muslims</a>; 15% were unaffiliated to any religion.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-40"><a href="#cite_note-40">[40]</a></sup></p>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Languages">Languages</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Shenzhen&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Languages">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Prior to the establishment of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Special_Economic_Zone" title="Special Economic Zone">Special Economic Zone</a>, the indigenous local communities could be divided into <a href="/wiki/Yue_Chinese" title="Yue Chinese">Cantonese</a> and <a href="/wiki/Hakka_Chinese" title="Hakka Chinese">Hakka</a> speakers,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-41"><a href="#cite_note-41">[41]</a></sup> which were two cultural and linguistic sub-ethnic groups vernacular to Guangdong province. Two Cantonese varieties were spoken locally. One was a fairly standard variety. The other, which was spoken by several villages south of Fuhua Rd. was called <a href="/wiki/Weitou_dialect" title="Weitou dialect">Weitou dialect</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-42"><a href="#cite_note-42">[42]</a></sup> Two or three Hong Kong villages south of the Shenzhen River also speak this dialect. This is consistent with the area settled by people who accompanied the Southern Song court to the south in the late 13th century.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-43"><a href="#cite_note-43">[43]</a></sup> Younger generations of the Cantonese communities now speak the more prestigious variety, known as <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Standard_Cantonese" title="Standard Cantonese">standard Cantonese</a>, probably because of the influence of Hong Kong broadcasting. Today, the original inhabitants of the Cantonese and Hakka speaking communities are dispersing into more recently built urban settlements (e.g. apartments and villas), but a large proportion of them are still clustering in their <a href="/wiki/Urban_village_(China)" title="Urban village (China)">traditional urban and suburban villages</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-44"><a href="#cite_note-44">[44]</a></sup></p>
<p>The influx of migrants from other parts of the country has drastically altered the city's linguistic landscape, as Shenzhen has undergone a <a href="/wiki/Language_shift" title="Language shift">language shift</a> towards <a href="/wiki/Mandarin_Chinese" title="Mandarin Chinese">Mandarin</a>, which was both promoted by the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Chinese_Central_Government" title="Chinese Central Government">Chinese Central Government</a> as a national <a href="/wiki/Lingua_franca" title="Lingua franca">lingua franca</a> and natively spoken by most of the out-of-province immigrants and their descendants.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-45"><a href="#cite_note-45">[45]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-46"><a href="#cite_note-46">[46]</a></sup> Since then, the Cantonese- and Hakka-speaking populations were diluted into trivial proportions. Despite the ubiquity of Mandarin Chinese, <a href="/wiki/Yue_Chinese" title="Yue Chinese">Cantonese</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hakka_Chinese" title="Hakka Chinese">Hakka</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Teochew_dialect" title="Teochew dialect">Teochew</a> are still spoken among people of in-province ancestries in private occasions to a lesser extent than Mandarin. <a href="/wiki/Hokkien" title="Hokkien">Hokkien</a> and <a href="/wiki/Xiang_Chinese" title="Xiang Chinese">Xiang</a> are also sometimes observed.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (December 2016)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<p>Mandarin native speakers, whose majority is out-of-province immigrants and their descendants are found unwilling to learn Cantonese, Hakka or Teochew, probably due to Mandarin's dominance, advantages, administrative legitimacy, educational priority, societal bias, and official statuses at international, national, provincial, and municipal levels,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-47"><a href="#cite_note-47">[47]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-48"><a href="#cite_note-48">[48]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-49"><a href="#cite_note-49">[49]</a></sup> as well as those languages' inherent complexities and difficulties. However, in recent years trilingualism is on the rise as descendants of immigrants begin to assimilate into the local culture through friends, television and other media.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-50"><a href="#cite_note-50">[50]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Economy">Economy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Shenzhen&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Economy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:ZTE_Shenzhen.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2112" data-file-width="2816" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fa/ZTE_Shenzhen.JPG/220px-ZTE_Shenzhen.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fa/ZTE_Shenzhen.JPG/330px-ZTE_Shenzhen.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fa/ZTE_Shenzhen.JPG/440px-ZTE_Shenzhen.JPG 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:ZTE_Shenzhen.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Shenzhen High-Tech Industrial Park</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Huawei_1.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1704" data-file-width="2126" height="176" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/73/Huawei_1.JPG/220px-Huawei_1.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/73/Huawei_1.JPG/330px-Huawei_1.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/73/Huawei_1.JPG/440px-Huawei_1.JPG 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Huawei_1.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The global headquarters of <a href="/wiki/Huawei" title="Huawei">Huawei</a> is located in <a href="/wiki/Longhua_District,_Shenzhen" title="Longhua District, Shenzhen">Longhua District, Shenzhen</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>In 2015, Shenzhen's GDP totaled $270 billion, putting it on par with a mid-sized province by terms of total GDP. Its total economic output is higher than that of Portugal, the Republic of Ireland, and Vietnam. Its per-capita GDP was ¥164,664 ($25,038) as of 2014<sup class="plainlinks noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Shenzhen&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, on par with some of the developed countries of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/OECD" title="OECD">OECD</a>. Shenzhen was the first of the Special Economic Zones to be established and it showed the most rapid growth, averaging at a very high growth rate of 40% per annum between 1981 and 1993, compared to the average GDP growth of 9.8% for the country as a whole.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-51"><a href="#cite_note-51">[51]</a></sup> The economic growth later slowed after this early breakneck pace; from 2001 to 2005, Shenzhen's overall GDP grew by 16.3 percent yearly on average, though growth has slowed to around 10% per year since 2012. Shenzhen is in the top ranks among mainland Chinese cities in terms of comprehensive economic power. Shenzhen's economic output is ranked fourth among the 659 Chinese cities (behind <a href="/wiki/Beijing" title="Beijing">Beijing</a>, <a href="/wiki/Shanghai" title="Shanghai">Shanghai</a> and <a href="/wiki/Guangzhou" title="Guangzhou">Guangzhou</a>).</p>
<p>In 2001, the working population reached 3.3 million. Though the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Secondary_sector_of_industry" title="Secondary sector of industry">secondary sector of industry</a> had the largest share (1.85 million in 2001, increased by 5.5%), the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tertiary_sector_of_industry" title="Tertiary sector of industry">tertiary sector of industry</a> is growing fast (1.44 million in 2001, increased by 11.6%). The proportion of the three industries to the aggregate of GDP was 0.1:46.7:53.2 in 2009. The proportion of the primary industry to GDP was down by 13.4%, and the tertiary industry was up by 12.5%.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-52"><a href="#cite_note-52">[52]</a></sup> Its import and export volumes have been first for the last nine consecutive years. It is the second in terms of industrial output. For five consecutive years, its internal revenue within local budget ranks third. It also ranks third in the use of foreign capital.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-53"><a href="#cite_note-53">[53]</a></sup></p>
<p>Shenzhen is a major <a href="/wiki/Manufacturing" title="Manufacturing">manufacturing</a> center in China. In the 1990s, Shenzhen was described as constructing "one high-rise a day and one boulevard every three days". The Shenzhen's rapidly growing skyline is regarded among the best in the world. It currently has 59 buildings at over 200 meters tall, including the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Kingkey_100" title="Kingkey 100">Kingkey 100</a> (the 14th tallest building in the world) and <a href="/wiki/Shun_Hing_Square" title="Shun Hing Square">Shun Hing Square</a> (the 19th tallest building in the world).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-54"><a href="#cite_note-54">[54]</a></sup></p>
<p>Shenzhen is home to some of China's most successful high-tech companies, including <a href="/wiki/BYD_Company" title="BYD Company">BYD</a>, <a href="/wiki/Konka_Group" title="Konka Group">Konka</a>, <a href="/wiki/Skyworth" title="Skyworth">Skyworth</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tencent_Holdings_Ltd" title="Tencent Holdings Ltd">Tencent</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Coolpad" title="Coolpad">Coolpad</a>, <a href="/wiki/ZTE" title="ZTE">ZTE</a>, <a href="/wiki/Gionee" title="Gionee">Gionee</a>, <a href="/wiki/TP-Link" title="TP-Link">TP-Link</a>, <a href="/wiki/DJI_(company)" title="DJI (company)">DJI</a>, <a href="/wiki/Beijing_Genomics_Institute" title="Beijing Genomics Institute">BGI (Beijing Genomics Institute)</a>, <a href="/wiki/OnePlus" title="OnePlus">OnePlus</a> and <a href="/wiki/Huawei" title="Huawei">Huawei</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-55"><a href="#cite_note-55">[55]</a></sup> Taiwan's largest company, <a href="/wiki/Foxconn" title="Foxconn">Hon Hai</a> Group, has a large manufacturing plant based in Shenzhen. Many foreign high-tech companies have their China operations centers located in the Science and Technology Park of the Nanshan District.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-56"><a href="#cite_note-56">[56]</a></sup> Additional examples of successful Chinese companies with large operation in Shenzhen include the <a href="/wiki/China_International_Marine_Containers" title="China International Marine Containers">China International Marine Containers</a>, the largest container-manufacturing company in the world,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-57"><a href="#cite_note-57">[57]</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Vanke" title="Vanke">Vanke</a> which is among the largest residential real estate developers in China.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-58"><a href="#cite_note-58">[58]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-59"><a href="#cite_note-59">[59]</a></sup> In the financial sector, <a href="/wiki/Ping_An_Bank" title="Ping An Bank">Ping An Bank</a> and <a href="/wiki/China_Merchants_Bank" title="China Merchants Bank">China Merchants Bank</a> are some of the largest banks in China, with headquarters in Shenzhen.</p>
<p>Due to its unique status, Shenzhen is also an extremely fertile ground for startups, be it by Chinese or foreign entrepreneurs. Successful startups include <a href="/wiki/Petcube" title="Petcube">Petcube</a>, Palette, WearVigo, Notch and Makeblock.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-60"><a href="#cite_note-60">[60]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-61"><a href="#cite_note-61">[61]</a></sup> Shenzhen is also the product development base of the hardware startup accelerator, <a href="/wiki/HAX_Accelerator" title="HAX Accelerator">HAX Accelerator</a> (formerly HAXLR8R).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-62"><a href="#cite_note-62">[62]</a></sup></p>
<p>Shenzhen Convention &amp; Exhibition Center is a large public construction project with multiple functions of hosting business activities, celebrations, conferences, conventions, entertainment events, exhibitions, restaurants and all kinds of shows.</p>
<p><b>SEZ Border</b></p>
<p>Land borders between Shenzhen SEZ and the rest of China has been set up since the establishment of the SEZ. The border was known as 二线关 (<a href="/wiki/Pinyin" title="Pinyin">pinyin</a>: <i><span lang="zh-Latn-pinyin">èr xiàn guān</span></i>).</p>
<p>Initially, the border control was relatively strict, and required mainland Chinese non-Shenzhen SEZ citizens to obtain special permissions for entering. Over the years, border controls have gradually weakened, and permission requirement has been abandoned.</p>
<p>On 1 July 2010, the distinction was broken, the original SEZ border control was cancelled, and the Shenzhen special economic zone was expanded to the whole city. The area of Shenzhen SEZ thus increased from 396 square kilometres (153 sq mi) to 1,953 square kilometres (754 sq mi).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-63"><a href="#cite_note-63">[63]</a></sup></p>
<p>Although the Shenzhen Special Economic Zone have been extended to cover the whole of Shenzhen, colloquially Shenzhen is still said to be separated into two areas, with the original four districts comprising the SEZ before 2010 as 关内 (<a href="/wiki/Pinyin" title="Pinyin">pinyin</a>: <i><span lang="zh-Latn-pinyin">guān nèi</span></i>; literally: "within the border") and the rest known as 关外 (<a href="/wiki/Pinyin" title="Pinyin">pinyin</a>: <i><span lang="zh-Latn-pinyin">guān wài</span></i>; literally: "outside of the border").<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-64"><a href="#cite_note-64">[64]</a></sup></p>
<p>Since June 2015 the existing unused border structures have been demolished and are being transformed into urban greenspaces and parks.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-65"><a href="#cite_note-65">[65]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-66"><a href="#cite_note-66">[66]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-67"><a href="#cite_note-67">[67]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Industrial_zones">Industrial zones</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Shenzhen&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Industrial zones">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<ul>
<li>Shenzhen Hi-Tech Industrial Park (SHIP) was founded in September 1996. It covers an area of 11.5 km<sup>2</sup> (4.4 sq mi). Industries encouraged in the zone include Biotechnology/Pharmaceuticals, Building/Construction Materials, Chemicals Production and Processing, Computer Software, Electronics Assembly &amp; Manufacturing, Instruments &amp; Industrial Equipment Production, Medical Equipment and Supplies, Research and Development, Telecommunications Equipment.</li>
<li>Shenzhen Software Park is integrated with Shenzhen Hi-Tech Industry Park, an important vehicle established by Shenzhen Municipal Government to support the development of software industry. The Park was approved to be the base of software production of the National Plan in 2001. The distance between the 010 National Highway and the zone is 20.8 km (12.9 mi). The zone is situated 22 km (14 mi) from the Shenzhen Bao'an International Airport.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-68"><a href="#cite_note-68">[68]</a></sup></li>
</ul>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Shenzhen_Stock_Exchange">Shenzhen Stock Exchange</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Shenzhen&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Shenzhen Stock Exchange">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Shenzhen_Stock_Exchange" title="Shenzhen Stock Exchange">Shenzhen Stock Exchange</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Shenzhen_Stock_Exchange_1-2014.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3294" data-file-width="4392" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/80/Shenzhen_Stock_Exchange_1-2014.jpg/220px-Shenzhen_Stock_Exchange_1-2014.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/80/Shenzhen_Stock_Exchange_1-2014.jpg/330px-Shenzhen_Stock_Exchange_1-2014.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/80/Shenzhen_Stock_Exchange_1-2014.jpg/440px-Shenzhen_Stock_Exchange_1-2014.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Shenzhen_Stock_Exchange_1-2014.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Shenzhen_Stock_Exchange" title="Shenzhen Stock Exchange">Shenzhen Stock Exchange</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The Shenzhen Stock Exchange (<i>SZSE</i>) is a mutualized national <a href="/wiki/Stock_exchange" title="Stock exchange">stock exchange</a> under the <a href="/wiki/China_Securities_Regulatory_Commission" title="China Securities Regulatory Commission">China Securities Regulatory Commission</a> (CSRC) that provides a venue for <a href="/wiki/Security_(finance)" title="Security (finance)">securities</a> trading.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-69"><a href="#cite_note-69">[69]</a></sup> A broad spectrum of market participants, including 540 <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Listed_company" title="Listed company">listed companies</a>, 35 million registered investors and 177 exchange members, create the market. Since its creation in 1990, the SZSE has grown with a <a href="/wiki/Market_capitalization" title="Market capitalization">market capitalization</a> around 1 trillion yuan (US$122 billion). On a daily basis, around 600,000 deals, valued at US$807 million, trade on the SZSE.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Integration_with_Hong_Kong">Integration with Hong Kong</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Shenzhen&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Integration with Hong Kong">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Shenzhen_Bay_Bridge_2.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="713" data-file-width="1600" height="98" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5e/Shenzhen_Bay_Bridge_2.jpg/220px-Shenzhen_Bay_Bridge_2.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5e/Shenzhen_Bay_Bridge_2.jpg/330px-Shenzhen_Bay_Bridge_2.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5e/Shenzhen_Bay_Bridge_2.jpg/440px-Shenzhen_Bay_Bridge_2.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Shenzhen_Bay_Bridge_2.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Shenzhen_Bay_Bridge" title="Shenzhen Bay Bridge">Shenzhen Bay Bridge</a> forms part of the Shenzhen Bay Port crossing, connecting <a href="/wiki/Dongjiaotou" title="Dongjiaotou">Dongjiaotou</a> in Shenzhen with Ngau Hom Shek in Hong Kong</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Hong Kong and Shenzhen have close business, trade and social links as demonstrated by the statistics presented below. Except where noted the statistics are taken from sections of the Hong Kong Government website.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-70"><a href="#cite_note-70">[70]</a></sup></p>
<p>As of September 2016, there are nine crossing points on the boundary between Shenzhen and Hong Kong, among which six are land connections. From west to east these include the <a href="/wiki/Shenzhen_Bay_Port" title="Shenzhen Bay Port">Shenzhen Bay Port</a>, <a href="/wiki/Futian_Port" title="Futian Port">Futian Port</a>, <a href="/wiki/Huanggang_Port" title="Huanggang Port">Huanggang Port</a>, <a href="/wiki/Man_Kam_To_Control_Point" title="Man Kam To Control Point">Man Kam To Port</a>, <a href="/wiki/Luohu_Port" title="Luohu Port">Luohu Port</a> and <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Shatoujiao_Port&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Shatoujiao Port (page does not exist)">Shatoujiao Port</a>. On either sides of each of these ports of entry are road and/or rail transportation.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-71"><a href="#cite_note-71">[71]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-HKG_Monthly_Digest_of_Statistics_72-0"><a href="#cite_note-HKG_Monthly_Digest_of_Statistics-72">[72]</a></sup></p>
<p>In 2006, there were around 20,500 daily vehicular crossings of the boundary in each direction. Of these 65 percent were cargo vehicles, 27 percent cars and the remainder buses and coaches. The Huanggang crossing was most heavily used at 76 percent of the total, followed by the Futian crossing at 18 percent and Shatoujiao at 6 percent.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-73"><a href="#cite_note-73">[73]</a></sup> Of the cargo vehicles, 12,000 per day were container carrying and, using a rate of 1.44 teus/vehicle, this results in 17,000 teus/day across the boundary,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-74"><a href="#cite_note-74">[74]</a></sup> while Hong Kong port handled 23,000 teus/day during 2006, excluding trans-shipment trade.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-75"><a href="#cite_note-75">[75]</a></sup></p>
<p>Trade with Hong Kong in 2006 consisted of US$333 billion of imports of which US$298 billion were re-exported. Of these figures 94 percent were associated with China.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-76"><a href="#cite_note-76">[76]</a></sup> Considering that 34.5 percent of the value of Hong Kong trade is air freight (only 1.3 percent by weight), a large proportion of this is associated with China as well.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-hongkongairport.com_77-0"><a href="#cite_note-hongkongairport.com-77">[77]</a></sup></p>
<p>Also in 2006 the average daily passenger flow through the four connections open at that time was over 200,000 in each direction of which 63 percent used the Luohu rail connection and 33 percent the Huanggang road connection.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-HKG_Monthly_Digest_of_Statistics_72-1"><a href="#cite_note-HKG_Monthly_Digest_of_Statistics-72">[72]</a></sup> Naturally, such high volumes require special handling, and the largest group of people crossing the boundary, Hong Kong residents with Chinese citizenship, use only a biometric ID card (<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Home_Return_Permit" title="Home Return Permit">Home Return Permit</a>) and a thumb print reader. As a point of comparison, Hong Kong’s Chek Lap Kok Airport, the 5th busiest international airport in the world, handled 59,000 passengers per day in each direction.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-hongkongairport.com_77-1"><a href="#cite_note-hongkongairport.com-77">[77]</a></sup></p>
<p>Hong Kong conducts regular surveys of cross-boundary passenger movements, with the most recent being in 2003, although the 2007 survey will be reported on soon<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Manual_of_Style/Dates_and_numbers#Chronological_items" title="Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Dates and numbers"><span title="The time period mentioned near this tag is ambiguous. (October 2014)">when?</span></a></i>]</sup>. In 2003 the boundary crossings for Hong Kong Residents living in Hong Kong made 78 percent of the trips, up by 33 percent from 1999, whereas Hong Kong and Chinese residents of China made up 20 percent in 2006, an increase of 140 percent above the 1999 figure. Since that time movement has been made much easier for China residents, and so that group have probably increased further still. Other nationalities made up 2 percent of boundary crossings. Of these trips 67 percent were associated with Shenzhen and 42 percent were for business or work purposes. Of the non-business trips about one third were to visit friends and relatives and the remainder for leisure.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-78"><a href="#cite_note-78">[78]</a></sup></p>
<p>After Shenzhen's attempts to be included in the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hong_Kong-Zhuhai-Macau_Bridge" title="Hong Kong-Zhuhai-Macau Bridge">Hong Kong-Zhuhai-Macau Bridge</a> project were rejected in 2004, a separate bridge was conceived connecting Shenzhen on the Eastern side of the Pearl River Delta with the city of <a href="/wiki/Zhongshan" title="Zhongshan">Zhongshan</a> on the Western side: the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Shenzhen-Zhongshan_Bridge" title="Shenzhen-Zhongshan Bridge">Shenzhen-Zhongshan Bridge</a>.</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Qianhai">Qianhai</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Shenzhen&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Qianhai">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Qianhai" title="Qianhai">Qianhai</a></div>
<p><a href="/wiki/Qianhai" title="Qianhai">Qianhai</a>, which means "foresea" in Chinese language, formally known as the Qianhai Shenzhen-Hong Kong Modern Service Industries Cooperation Zone, is "a useful exploration for China to create a new opening up layout with a more open economic system."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-nzcta.co.nz_79-0"><a href="#cite_note-nzcta.co.nz-79">[79]</a></sup> A 15 km² area located in western Shenzhen, Qianhai lies at the heart of the Pearl River Delta, adjacent to Shenzhen international airport. Strategically positioned as a zone for the innovation and development of modern services, Qianhai will facilitate closer cooperation between Hong Kong and mainland China, as well as act as the catalyst for industrial reform in the Pearl River Delta.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-80"><a href="#cite_note-80">[80]</a></sup> With the goal of loosening capital account restrictions, Qianhai authorities have indicated that Hong Kong banks will be allowed to extend commercial RMB loans to Qianhai-based onshore mainland entities. The People's Bank of China has also indicated that such loans will for the first time not be subject to the benchmark rates set by the central bank for all other loans in the rest of China. According to Anita Fung from <a href="/wiki/HSBC" title="HSBC">HSBC</a>, "This new measure on cross-border lending will enhance the co-operation between Hong Kong and Shenzhen and accelerate cross-border convergence."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-nzcta.co.nz_79-1"><a href="#cite_note-nzcta.co.nz-79">[79]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Cityscape">Cityscape</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Shenzhen&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Cityscape">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/List_of_tallest_buildings_in_Shenzhen" title="List of tallest buildings in Shenzhen">List of tallest buildings in Shenzhen</a></div>
<p>The tallest building in Shenzhen is <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Kingkey_100" title="Kingkey 100">Kingkey 100</a>, rising 441.8 metres (1,449 ft) and containing 100 floors of office and hotel spaces.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-skyscraperCenter_81-0"><a href="#cite_note-skyscraperCenter-81">[81]</a></sup> Shenzhen is also the home to the <a href="/wiki/Shun_Hing_Square" title="Shun Hing Square">Shun Hing Square</a> (Diwang Building), the tallest in Asia (if the antenna is taken into account) when it was built in 1996.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-82"><a href="#cite_note-82">[82]</a></sup> The city has 59 buildings over 200 m (656 ft) built and topped out, and 9 of them are over 300 m (980 ft),<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-83"><a href="#cite_note-83">[83]</a></sup> mostly concentrated in <a href="/wiki/Nanshan_District,_Shenzhen" title="Nanshan District, Shenzhen">Nanshan</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Luohu" title="Luohu">Luohu</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Futian" title="Futian">Futian</a> districts. The third tallest building in Shenzhen is <a href="/wiki/SEG_Plaza" title="SEG Plaza">SEG Plaza</a> at a height of 356 meters (291.6 meters to roof-top<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-skyscraperCenter1_84-0"><a href="#cite_note-skyscraperCenter1-84">[84]</a></sup>), located in <a href="/wiki/Huaqiangbei" title="Huaqiangbei">Huaqiangbei</a>. <a href="/wiki/Guomao_Building" title="Guomao Building">Guomao Building</a> was furthermore the tallest building in China when it was completed in 1985.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-85"><a href="#cite_note-85">[85]</a></sup></p>
<p>A number of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Supertall" title="Supertall">supertalls</a> that have been either proposed, approved or under construction are well over 400 m (1,312 ft). The tallest among these supertalls under construction is the 599-meter <a href="/wiki/Ping_An_Finance_Centre" title="Ping An Finance Centre">Ping An Finance Centre</a>, which will become the <a href="/wiki/List_of_tallest_buildings_in_China" title="List of tallest buildings in China">second tallest in China</a> and the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/List_of_tallest_buildings_in_the_world" title="List of tallest buildings in the world">fourth tallest building in the world</a> upon its scheduled completion in 2016.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-86"><a href="#cite_note-86">[86]</a></sup></p>
