<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Transport">Transport</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Shenzhen&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Transport">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Transport_in_Shenzhen" title="Transport in Shenzhen">Transport in Shenzhen</a></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Road">Road</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Shenzhen&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Road">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">See also: <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/List_of_roads_in_Shenzhen" title="List of roads in Shenzhen">List of roads in Shenzhen</a></div>
<p>Since February 2003, the road border crossing at <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Huanggang,_Shenzhen" title="Huanggang, Shenzhen">Huanggang</a> and <a href="/wiki/Lok_Ma_Chau" title="Lok Ma Chau">Lok Ma Chau</a> in Hong Kong has been open 24 hours a day. The journey can be made by private vehicle or by bus. On 15 August 2007, the Lok Ma Chau-Huanggang pedestrian border crossing opened, linking <a href="/wiki/Lok_Ma_Chau_Station" title="Lok Ma Chau Station">Lok Ma Chau Station</a> with Huanggang. With the opening of the crossing, shuttle buses between Lok Ma Chau transport interchange and Huanggang were terminated.</p>
<p>The planned <a href="/wiki/Shenzhen%E2%80%93Zhongshan_Bridge" title="Shenzhen–Zhongshan Bridge">Shenzhen–Zhongshan Bridge</a> will connect Shenzhen on the Eastern side of the Pearl River Delta with the city of <a href="/wiki/Zhongshan" title="Zhongshan">Zhongshan</a> on the Western side. It will consist of a series of bridges and tunnels, starting from Bao'an International Airport on the Shenzhen side. Construction of the proposed 51 km (32 mi) eight-lane link is scheduled to start in 2015, with completion scheduled for 2021.</p>
<p>Taxis are metered and come in four colors. The red taxis may travel throughout the city. The green taxis are restricted to travel outside of the original Shenzhen <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Special_Economic_Zones_of_China" title="Special Economic Zones of China">Special Economic Zone (SEZ)</a> (Futian, Nanshan, Luohu and Yantian districts). Conversely, the less-common yellow taxis charging the same as red ones, runs only within the original Shenzhen SEZ. A recently introduced electric-powered taxi costs similar to the red and yellow ones, only having no fuel surcharge levied on.</p>
<p>There are also frequent bus and van services from Hong Kong International Airport to Huanggang and most major hotels in Shenzhen. A bus service operated by Chinalink Bus Company operates from <a href="/wiki/Kowloon_Station_(MTR)" title="Kowloon Station (MTR)">Kowloon Station</a> on the <a href="/wiki/Airport_Express_(MTR)" title="Airport Express (MTR)">Airport Express</a> <a href="/wiki/MTR" title="MTR">MTR</a> line (below <a href="/wiki/Elements,_Hong_Kong" title="Elements, Hong Kong">Elements Mall</a>) direct to the <a href="/wiki/Shenzhen_Bao%27an_International_Airport" title="Shenzhen Bao'an International Airport">Shenzhen International airport</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-87"><a href="#cite_note-87">[87]</a></sup></p>
<p>As of 29 December 2014, Shenzhen banned passenger vehicles with license plates issued in other places from four of Shenzhen's main districts during peak times on working days.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-88"><a href="#cite_note-88">[88]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Port">Port</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Shenzhen&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Port">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Port_of_Shenzhen" title="Port of Shenzhen">Port of Shenzhen</a></div>
<p>The city's 260-kilometre (162 mi) coastline is divided by the main landmass of Hong Kong (namely the <a href="/wiki/New_Territories" title="New Territories">New Territories</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Kowloon_Peninsula" title="Kowloon Peninsula">Kowloon Peninsula</a>) into two halves, the eastern and the western. Shenzhen’s western port area lies to the east of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Pearl_River_estuary" title="Pearl River estuary">Lingdingyang</a> in the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Pearl_River_Estuary" title="Pearl River Estuary">Pearl River Estuary</a> and possesses a deep water harbour with superb natural shelters. It is about 20 nautical miles (40 km) from Hong Kong to the south and 60 nautical miles (110 km) from Guangzhou to the north. By passing Pearl River system, the western port area is connected with the cities and counties in Pearl River Delta networks; by passing <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=On_See_Dun&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="On See Dun (page does not exist)">On See Dun</a> waterway, it extends all ports both at home and abroad.</p>
<p>Shenzhen handled a record number of <a href="/wiki/Containerization" title="Containerization">containers</a> in 2005, ranking as the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/List_of_largest_ports" title="List of largest ports">world's third-busiest port</a>, after rising trade increased cargo shipments through the city. <a href="/wiki/China_International_Marine_Containers" title="China International Marine Containers">China International Marine Containers</a>, and other operators of the port handled 16.2 million standard 20-foot (6.1 m) boxes last year, a 19 per cent increase. Investors in Shenzhen are expanding to take advantage of rising volume.</p>
<p><a href="/wiki/Yantian_International_Container_Terminals" title="Yantian International Container Terminals">Yantian International Container Terminals</a>, <a href="/wiki/Chiwan" title="Chiwan">Chiwan</a> <a href="/wiki/Container_terminal" title="Container terminal">Container terminals</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Shekou_Industrial_Zone" title="Shekou Industrial Zone">Shekou</a> Container Terminals, <a href="/wiki/China_Merchants_Port" title="China Merchants Port">China Merchants Port</a> and <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Shenzhen_Haixing&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Shenzhen Haixing (page does not exist)">Shenzhen Haixing</a> (Mawan port) are the major port terminals in Shenzhen.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-89"><a href="#cite_note-89">[89]</a></sup></p>
<div style="clear:both;"></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Air">Air</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Shenzhen&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Air">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Shenzhen_Bao%27an_International_Airport" title="Shenzhen Bao'an International Airport">Shenzhen Bao'an International Airport</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Shenzhen_Bao%27an_Airport.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3265" data-file-width="7176" height="100" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8d/Shenzhen_Bao%27an_Airport.jpg/220px-Shenzhen_Bao%27an_Airport.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8d/Shenzhen_Bao%27an_Airport.jpg/330px-Shenzhen_Bao%27an_Airport.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8d/Shenzhen_Bao%27an_Airport.jpg/440px-Shenzhen_Bao%27an_Airport.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Shenzhen_Bao%27an_Airport.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Shenzhen airport T3</div>
</div>
</div>
<p><a href="/wiki/Shenzhen_Airlines" title="Shenzhen Airlines">Shenzhen Airlines</a> and <a href="/wiki/Jade_Cargo_International" title="Jade Cargo International">Jade Cargo International</a> are located at <a href="/wiki/Shenzhen_Bao%27an_International_Airport" title="Shenzhen Bao'an International Airport">Shenzhen Bao'an International Airport</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-90"><a href="#cite_note-90">[90]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-91"><a href="#cite_note-91">[91]</a></sup> The airport is 35 kilometres (22 miles) from central Shenzhen and connects the city with many other parts of China, and serves domestic and international destinations. The airport also serves as an Asian-Pacific cargo hub for <a href="/wiki/UPS_Airlines" title="UPS Airlines">UPS Airlines</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-autogenerated2_92-0"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated2-92">[92]</a></sup> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Shenzhen_Donghai_Airlines" title="Shenzhen Donghai Airlines">Shenzhen Donghai Airlines</a> has its head office in the Shenzhen Airlines facility on the airport property.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-93"><a href="#cite_note-93">[93]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/SF_Airlines" title="SF Airlines">SF Airlines</a> has its headquarters in the International Shipping Center.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-94"><a href="#cite_note-94">[94]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Railway">Railway</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Shenzhen&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Railway">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Shenzhen_Railway_Station_2008.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1600" data-file-width="1200" height="293" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4a/Shenzhen_Railway_Station_2008.jpg/220px-Shenzhen_Railway_Station_2008.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4a/Shenzhen_Railway_Station_2008.jpg/330px-Shenzhen_Railway_Station_2008.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4a/Shenzhen_Railway_Station_2008.jpg/440px-Shenzhen_Railway_Station_2008.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Shenzhen_Railway_Station_2008.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
View from Shenzhen Railway Station</div>
</div>
</div>
<p><a href="/wiki/Shenzhen_Railway_Station" title="Shenzhen Railway Station">Shenzhen Railway Station</a> is located at the junction of Jianshe Road, Heping Road and Renmin Nan Road and provides links to different parts of China. There are frequent <a href="/wiki/China_Railway_High-speed" title="China Railway High-speed">high speed</a> trains to Guangzhou, plus long-distance trains to Beijing, Shanghai, Changsha, Jiujiang, Maoming, Shantou and other destinations. The train from Hong Kong's <a href="/wiki/Hung_Hom" title="Hung Hom">Hung Hom</a> <a href="/wiki/MTR" title="MTR">MTR</a> station to the <a href="/wiki/Lo_Wu" title="Lo Wu">Lo Wu</a> and <a href="/wiki/Lok_Ma_Chau" title="Lok Ma Chau">Lok Ma Chau</a> border crossings take 43 minutes and 45 minutes respectively.</p>
<p><a href="/wiki/Shenzhen_West_Railway_Station" title="Shenzhen West Railway Station">Shenzhen West Station</a> is located at <a href="/wiki/Qianhai" title="Qianhai">Qianhai</a>, <a href="/wiki/Nanshan_District,_Shenzhen" title="Nanshan District, Shenzhen">Nanshan</a>.This station is used for a small number of long distance trains, such as ones to <a href="/wiki/Hefei" title="Hefei">Hefei</a>.</p>
<p><a href="/wiki/Shenzhen_North_Railway_Station" title="Shenzhen North Railway Station">Shenzhen North Railway Station</a> opened in 2011 in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Longhua_New_District" title="Longhua New District">Longhua</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-95"><a href="#cite_note-95">[95]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-96"><a href="#cite_note-96">[96]</a></sup> The station is currently handling high-speed trains to Guangzhou South, Guangzhou North, Changsha, Wuhan, Beijing and intermediate stations on the Beijing-Guangzhou-Shenzhen-Hong Kong HSR route.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-97"><a href="#cite_note-97">[97]</a></sup></p>
<p>Shenzhen East Railway Station was opened in December 2012. It was originally called Buji station after the suburb it is located and was a Grade 3 station along the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Guangshen_Railway" title="Guangshen Railway">Guangshen Railway</a> with no passenger services. Now after massive renovations, it currently handles mostly regional services.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-98"><a href="#cite_note-98">[98]</a></sup></p>
<p><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Pingshan_Railway_Station" title="Pingshan Railway Station">Pingshan Railway Station</a> is completed in 2013 to serve high-speed trains on the Xiamen-Shenzhen HSR route opened in 2013.</p>
<p><a href="/wiki/Futian_Railway_Station" title="Futian Railway Station">Futian Railway Station</a> was completed by the end of 2015. It is completely underground, located in the centre of its namesake Futian District. The central location means it will become the focal point for most high-speed train services on the Beijing-Guangzhou-Shenzhen-Hong Kong HSR route upon completion. Connection to West Kowloon Railway Station in Hong Kong is scheduled to be completed in late 2018, allowing for 15 minute cross-border train journeys.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Metro">Metro</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Shenzhen&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Metro">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Shenzhen_Metro" title="Shenzhen Metro">Shenzhen Metro</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:SZMetro_RtDig.png"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3000" data-file-width="3500" height="189" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a4/SZMetro_RtDig.png/220px-SZMetro_RtDig.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a4/SZMetro_RtDig.png/330px-SZMetro_RtDig.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a4/SZMetro_RtDig.png/440px-SZMetro_RtDig.png 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:SZMetro_RtDig.png" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Map of Shenzhen Metro (excluding the newly opened Line 11 and Lines 7 and 9, scheduled to open in late 2016)</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Shenzhen_Metro" title="Shenzhen Metro">Shenzhen Metro</a> system opened on 28 December 2004. Phase I has only two lines: the Luobao and Longhua lines. Luobao line is from Luohu (Lo Wu and Shenzhen railway stations) to the <a href="/wiki/Window_of_the_World" title="Window of the World">Window of the World</a> (Overseas Chinese Town). The Longhua line is from Futian Kouan (Futian checkpoint; it was named Huang Gang at first) to Shaonian Gong (Children's Palace). The Shenzhen Metro currently has 6 lines, 149 stations, and 260 kilometres (160 mi)<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-.23_of_stations_99-0"><a href="#cite_note-.23_of_stations-99">[99]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-2011gongbao_100-0"><a href="#cite_note-2011gongbao-100">[100]</a></sup> of total trackage in operation.</p>
<p>In June 2011, the Shenzhen Metro extended the Luobao and Longhua lines. The Luobao line runs from Luohu to Shenzhen Bao'an Airport and the Longhua line (now operated by <a href="/wiki/MTR" title="MTR">MTR</a>) runs from Futian Kouan (Futian Checkpoint) to Qinghu. Also in June 2011, three lines of the second phase opened before the 26th summer <a href="/wiki/Universiade" title="Universiade">Universiade</a>. They are <a href="/wiki/Line_2,_Shenzhen_Metro" title="Line 2, Shenzhen Metro">Line 2</a> (Shekou line) (from <a href="/wiki/Chiwan_Station" title="Chiwan Station">Chiwan</a> to <a href="/wiki/Xinxiu_Station" title="Xinxiu Station">Xinxiu</a>), <a href="/wiki/Line_3,_Shenzhen_Metro" title="Line 3, Shenzhen Metro">Line 3</a> (Longgang line) (from <a href="/wiki/Yitian_Station" title="Yitian Station">Yitian</a> to <a href="/wiki/Shuanglong_Station_(Shenzhen)" title="Shuanglong Station (Shenzhen)">Shuanglong</a>), and <a href="/wiki/Line_5,_Shenzhen_Metro" title="Line 5, Shenzhen Metro">Line 5</a> (Huanzhong line) (from <a href="/wiki/Qianhaiwan_Station" title="Qianhaiwan Station">Qianhaiwan</a> to <a href="/wiki/Huangbeiling_Station" title="Huangbeiling Station">Huangbeiling</a>).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Under_Construction_101-0"><a href="#cite_note-Under_Construction-101">[101]</a></sup> Line 11 opened in June 2016, while Lines <a href="/wiki/Line_7,_Shenzhen_Metro" title="Line 7, Shenzhen Metro">7</a> and <a href="/wiki/Line_9,_Shenzhen_Metro" title="Line 9, Shenzhen Metro">9</a> will also open later in the year.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-102"><a href="#cite_note-102">[102]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Sea">Sea</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Shenzhen&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Sea">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Shekou_Passenger_Terminal" title="Shekou Passenger Terminal">Shekou Passenger Terminal</a></div>
<p>Shekou Passenger Terminal in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Shekou,_Shenzhen" title="Shekou, Shenzhen">Shekou</a> provides regular ferry transport to and from <a href="/wiki/Zhuhai" title="Zhuhai">Zhuhai</a>, <a href="/wiki/Macau" title="Macau">Macau</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hong_Kong_International_Airport" title="Hong Kong International Airport">Hong Kong International Airport</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kowloon" title="Kowloon">Kowloon</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Hong_Kong_Island" title="Hong Kong Island">Hong Kong Island</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-103"><a href="#cite_note-103">[103]</a></sup></p>
<p>Fuyong Passenger Terminal in <a href="/wiki/Bao%27an_District" title="Bao'an District">Bao'an</a> near <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Shenzhen_Airport" title="Shenzhen Airport">the airport</a> provide services to and from Hong Kong (Hong Kong International Airport) and Macau(<a href="/wiki/Taipa_Temporary_Ferry_Terminal" title="Taipa Temporary Ferry Terminal">Taipa Temporary Ferry Terminal</a> and <a href="/wiki/Outer_Harbour_Ferry_Terminal" title="Outer Harbour Ferry Terminal">Outer Harbour Ferry Terminal</a>)<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-104"><a href="#cite_note-104">[104]</a></sup></p>
<div style="clear:both;"></div>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Environment">Environment</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Shenzhen&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Environment">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Tourist_destinations.2C_parks_and_resorts">Tourist destinations, parks and resorts</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Shenzhen&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Tourist destinations, parks and resorts">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/List_of_parks_in_Shenzhen" title="List of parks in Shenzhen">List of parks in Shenzhen</a></div>
<p>Major tourist attractions of Shenzhen include the <a href="/wiki/China_Folk_Culture_Village" title="China Folk Culture Village">China Folk Culture Village</a>, <a href="/wiki/Window_of_the_World" title="Window of the World">Window of the World</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Happy_Valley,_Shenzhen" title="Happy Valley, Shenzhen">Happy Valley</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Splendid_China" title="Splendid China">Splendid China</a>, the Safari Park in Nanshan district, <a href="/wiki/Chung_Ying_Street" title="Chung Ying Street">Chung Ying Street</a>(a street dividing Shenzhen and <a href="/wiki/Sha_Tau_Kok" title="Sha Tau Kok">Sha Tau Kok</a>, Hong Kong), Xianhu Botanical Gardens, <a href="/wiki/Minsk_World" title="Minsk World">Minsk World</a>, amongst others. The city also offers free admission to over twenty public city parks <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-105"><a href="#cite_note-105">[105]</a></sup> including <a href="/wiki/People%27s_Park_(Shenzhen)" title="People's Park (Shenzhen)">People's Park</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lianhuashan_Park" title="Lianhuashan Park">Lianhuashan Park</a>, Lizhi Park, <a href="/wiki/Zhongshan_Park" title="Zhongshan Park">Zhongshan Park</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Mount_Wutong" title="Mount Wutong">Wutongshan Park</a>.</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Overseas_Chinese_Town_.28OCT.29">Overseas Chinese Town (OCT)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Shenzhen&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Overseas Chinese Town (OCT)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Overseas_Chinese_Town" title="Overseas Chinese Town">Overseas Chinese Town</a></div>
<p>The OCT East (东部华侨城) development in <a href="/wiki/Yantian_District" title="Yantian District">Yantian District</a> is also an events hotspot, featuring the Ecoventure Valley (大侠谷) and the Tea Stream Resort Valley (茶溪谷) theme parks, three scenic themed towns, two 18-hole golf courses and eight themed hotels. <a href="/wiki/OCT_East" title="OCT East">OCT East</a> was joined in 2012 by the <a href="/wiki/OCT_Bay" title="OCT Bay">OCT Bay</a> (欢乐海岸) development in <a href="/wiki/Nanshan_District,_Shenzhen" title="Nanshan District, Shenzhen">Nanshan</a>, which brought more attractions including an exhibition center, hotels and residences, an artificial beach called CoCo Beach, and an IMAX cinema.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-106"><a href="#cite_note-106">[106]</a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Shekou">Shekou</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Shenzhen&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Shekou">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Shekou" title="Shekou">Shekou</a></div>
<p>Shekou is a former industrial zone with a largely expatriate residential community, also home to a large shopping district called Sea World (海上世界) where a former French cruise liner <a href="/wiki/Minghua_(ship)" title="Minghua (ship)">Minghua</a> (明华), (known in French formerly as <i>MS Ancerville</i>) is cemented into the ground to become a hotel complex.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-107"><a href="#cite_note-107">[107]</a></sup> Shekou was expanded and renovated in recent years, partially via <a href="/wiki/Land_reclamation" title="Land reclamation">land reclamation</a>.</p>

<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Beaches">Beaches</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Shenzhen&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: Beaches">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>Beaches in Shenzhen include <a href="/wiki/Dameisha_Beach" title="Dameisha Beach">Dameisha</a> and Xiaomeisha in <a href="/wiki/Yantian_District" title="Yantian District">Yantian</a> and Xichong Beach in the south of <a href="/wiki/Dapeng_Peninsula" title="Dapeng Peninsula">Dapeng Peninsula</a>.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Museums_and_exhibitions">Museums and exhibitions</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Shenzhen&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: Museums and exhibitions">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<ul>
<li><a href="/wiki/Shenzhen_Convention_and_Exhibition_Center" title="Shenzhen Convention and Exhibition Center">Shenzhen Convention and Exhibition Center</a></li>
<li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Shenzhen_Civic_Center" title="Shenzhen Civic Center">Shenzhen Civic Center</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Shenzhen_Cultural_Center" title="Shenzhen Cultural Center">Shenzhen Cultural Center</a>, where the city's Central Music Hall and library are located</li>
</ul>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Media">Media</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Shenzhen&amp;action=edit&amp;section=30" title="Edit section: Media">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>The famous <a href="/wiki/Shenzhen_Daily" title="Shenzhen Daily">Shenzhen Daily</a> is the news outlet for Shenzhen. It also covers local, national and international news.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Sports">Sports</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Shenzhen&amp;action=edit&amp;section=31" title="Edit section: Sports">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<table class="plainlinks metadata ambox mbox-small-left ambox-content" role="presentation">
<tr>
<td class="mbox-image"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg"><img alt="[icon]" data-file-height="31" data-file-width="44" height="14" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1c/Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg/20px-Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1c/Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg/30px-Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1c/Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg/40px-Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg.png 2x" width="20"/></a></td>

</tr>
</table>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Shenzhen_Stadium.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2592" data-file-width="3888" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1d/Shenzhen_Stadium.jpg/220px-Shenzhen_Stadium.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1d/Shenzhen_Stadium.jpg/330px-Shenzhen_Stadium.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1d/Shenzhen_Stadium.jpg/440px-Shenzhen_Stadium.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Shenzhen_Stadium.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Shenzhen_Stadium" title="Shenzhen Stadium">Shenzhen Stadium</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The planned <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Shenzhen_Universiade_Sports_Center_Gymnasium&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Shenzhen Universiade Sports Center Gymnasium (page does not exist)">Shenzhen Universiade Sports Center Gymnasium</a> will be one of the venues for the <a href="/wiki/2019_FIBA_Basketball_World_Cup" title="2019 FIBA Basketball World Cup">2019 FIBA Basketball World Cup</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-108"><a href="#cite_note-108">[108]</a></sup></p>
<p>Shenzhen has two local football clubs, <a href="/wiki/Shenzhen_F.C." title="Shenzhen F.C.">Shenzhen F.C.</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Shenzhen_Renren_F.C." title="Shenzhen Renren F.C.">Shenzhen Renren F.C.</a>, who both play home games at the 40,000 capacity <a href="/wiki/Bao%27an_Stadium" title="Bao'an Stadium">Bao'an Stadium</a>. Shenzhen F.C. was one of the earliest professional football clubs in <a href="/wiki/Guangdong" title="Guangdong">Guangdong</a>, originally owned by memberships, later turned to shareholding.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-109"><a href="#cite_note-109">[109]</a></sup> The team won <a href="/wiki/Chinese_Super_League" title="Chinese Super League">Chinese Super League</a> title in <a href="/wiki/2004_Chinese_Super_League" title="2004 Chinese Super League">2004 season</a> despite severe financial problems leaving players unpaid for seven months.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-110"><a href="#cite_note-110">[110]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-111"><a href="#cite_note-111">[111]</a></sup> The team currently plays in <a href="/wiki/China_League_One" title="China League One">China League One</a>, the second tier of Chinese football competition system.</p>
<p><a href="/wiki/Shenzhen_Stadium" title="Shenzhen Stadium">Shenzhen Stadium</a> is a multi-purpose stadium that hosts many events. The stadium is located in <a href="/wiki/Futian_District" title="Futian District">Futian District</a> and has a capacity of 32,500. It was built in June 1993, at a cost of 141 million RMB. The <a href="/wiki/2011_Summer_Universiade" title="2011 Summer Universiade">26th Summer Universiade</a> was held in Shenzhen in August 2011.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-112"><a href="#cite_note-112">[112]</a></sup> Shenzhen has constructed the sports venues for this first major sporting event in the city.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-113"><a href="#cite_note-113">[113]</a></sup></p>
<p>Shenzhen is also a popular destination for skateboarders from all over the world, due to the architecture of the city and its lax skate laws.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-114"><a href="#cite_note-114">[114]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Education">Education</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Shenzhen&amp;action=edit&amp;section=32" title="Edit section: Education">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Colleges_and_universities">Colleges and universities</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Shenzhen&amp;action=edit&amp;section=33" title="Edit section: Colleges and universities">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="International_schools">International schools</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Shenzhen&amp;action=edit&amp;section=34" title="Edit section: International schools">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<ul>
<li><a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Vanke_Meisha_Academy&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Vanke Meisha Academy (page does not exist)">Vanke Meisha Academy</a></li>

<tr>
<th class="navbox-title" colspan="2" scope="col" style=";"><span style="float:left;width:6em"> </span>
<div id="Notes" style="font-size:114%"><small>Notes</small></div>
</th>
</tr>
<tr style="height:2px">
<td colspan="2"></td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td class="navbox-list navbox-odd" colspan="2" style="width:100%;padding:0px">
<div style="padding:0em 0.25em"></div>
<table class="nowraplinks navbox-subgroup" style="border-spacing:0">
<tr>
<td class="navbox-list navbox-odd" colspan="2" style="width:100%;padding:0px">
<div style="padding:0em 0.25em">* Indicates this city has already occurred above.<br/>
<p><sup>a</sup><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Direct-controlled_municipality_of_China" title="Direct-controlled municipality of China">Direct-controlled Municipalities</a>. <sup>b</sup><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sub-provincial_city_in_the_People%27s_Republic_of_China" title="Sub-provincial city in the People's Republic of China">Sub-provincial cities as provincial capitals</a>. <sup>c</sup><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sub-provincial_city_in_the_People%27s_Republic_of_China" title="Sub-provincial city in the People's Republic of China">Separate state-planning cities</a>. <sup>1</sup><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Special_Economic_Zones_of_China" title="Special Economic Zones of China">Special Economic Zone Cities</a>. <sup>2</sup><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Special_Economic_Zones_of_China" title="Special Economic Zones of China">Coastal development cities</a>.<br/>
<sup>3</sup>Prefecture capital status established by Heilongjiang Province and not recognized by Ministry of Civil Affairs. Disputed by <a href="/wiki/Oroqen_Autonomous_Banner" title="Oroqen Autonomous Banner">Oroqen Autonomous Banner</a>, Hulunbuir, Inner Mongolia as part of it.<br/>
<sup>4</sup>Only administers islands and waters in South China Sea and have no urban core comparable to typical cities in China.<br/>
<sup>5</sup>The claimed province of <a href="/wiki/Taiwan_Province,_People%27s_Republic_of_China" title="Taiwan Province, People's Republic of China">Taiwan</a> no longer have any internal division announced by Ministry of Civil Affairs of PRC, due to lack of actual jurisdiction. See <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Template:Administrative_divisions_of_the_Republic_of_China" title="Template:Administrative divisions of the Republic of China">Template:Administrative divisions of the Republic of China</a> instead.<br/></p>
All provincial capitals are listed first in prefecture-level cities by province.</div>

<td style="padding:0px;padding-left:0.25em;;;;width:20%;">
<div>
<ol style="margin-left:2.5em">
